  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dd7f33f5-593a-411c-9275-8b731293d064'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17572801126756612568">Intention is generally viewed as a pit-bull kind of determination propelling one to succeed at all costs by never giving up on an inner picture. In this view, an attitude that combines hard work with an indefatigable drive toward excellence is the way to succeed. However, intention is viewed very differently in this book. <b>Dr. Wayne W. Dyer </b>has researched intention as a for</span>
  <span id="freeText17572801126756612568" style="display:none">Intention is generally viewed as a pit-bull kind of determination propelling one to succeed at all costs by never giving up on an inner picture. In this view, an attitude that combines hard work with an indefatigable drive toward excellence is the way to succeed. However, intention is viewed very differently in this book. <b>Dr. Wayne W. Dyer </b>has researched intention as a force in the universe that <i>allows</i> the act of creation to take place. This book explores intention—not as something you do—but as an energy you’re a part of. We’re all <i>intended</i> here through the invisible power of intention. This is the first book to look at intention as a field of energy that you can access to begin co-creating your life with the power of intention.<br /> <br />Part I deals with the principles of intention, offering true stories and examples on ways to make the connection. Dr. Dyer identifies the attributes of the all-creating universal mind of intention as creative, kind, loving, beautiful, expanding, endlessly abundant, and receptive, explaining the importance of emulating this source of creativity. In Part II, Dr. Dyer offers an intention guide with specific ways to apply the co-creating principles in daily life. Part III is an exhilarating description of Dr. Dyer’s vision of a world in harmony with the universal mind of intention.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17572801126756612568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/31118321-karenbeth-glunz"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1522420921i/31118321._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/31118321-karenbeth-glunz">Karenbeth Glunz</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Your perspective of "failed" marriages depends upon other beliefs that are truly antiquated. Staying together "forever" is truly a fable and based on <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Your perspective of "failed" marriages depends upon other beliefs that are truly antiquated. Staying together "forever" is truly a fable and based on romantic love rather than true love. When I separated from my husband, I loved him dearly yet we had completed our time together. His desires were to buy a home (I did't want to purchase a home) in an area that he wanted to live (where I never wanted to live). . He then fell in love with another woman and we decided to go our separate ways. I wanted him to be happy. Six year later, he has the home that he wanted in the area that he wanted to live and a beautiful woman for his wife.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4066313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6774135083605419224">I took this book out from the library and ended up buying a copy of it so I could just have it and refer to it whenever I wanted to. I plan on reading it all over again here soon. It's fabulous! While I haven't read the "The Secret," from what I can gather from the reviews, this is pretty similar and is the "real stuff" without all the marketing fluff. </span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16523160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11700711593114340294">Although I think Wayne Dyer is discounted as a bit of a crackpot by some and he has clearly stretched out one idea and managed to turn it into several books/cds/seminars/manuals, I do find his thoughts helpful and even uplifting. I have to space him out in my reading/listening because he does get monotonous; however, I feel he has overall good intentions (pun intended)and I think I'll continue to be a follower.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6526650372375313704">“Good morning, This is God. I will be handling all of your problems today. I will not need your help, so have a miraculous day.” <br/><br/>“Say to yourself, ‘I’m here on purpose, I can accomplish anything I desire, and I do it by being in harmony with the all pervading creative force in the universe.’”<br/><br/>“One of the most effective means for transcending ordinary and moving into the realm of extraordinary is saying yes more frequently and eliminating no almost completely.   <span id="freeText6526650372375313704" style="display:none">“Good morning, This is God. I will be handling all of your problems today. I will not need your help, so have a miraculous day.” <br /><br />“Say to yourself, ‘I’m here on purpose, I can accomplish anything I desire, and I do it by being in harmony with the all pervading creative force in the universe.’”<br /><br />“One of the most effective means for transcending ordinary and moving into the realm of extraordinary is saying yes more frequently and eliminating no almost completely. I call it saying yes to life. Say yes to yourself, to your family, your children, your coworkers, and your business…”<br /><br />~ Wayne Dyer from The Power of Intention<br /><br />Wayne Dyer is one of my absolute favorite teachers. In fact, in my spiritual family tree he’s right there below Maslow in the spiritual dad spot (a position he shares with several peeps)! <br /><br />Have you ever heard about the effects of kindness on your brain? Dyer shares the amazing science of kindness in The Power of Intention. It goes something like this: <br /><br />Serotonin is the drug that makes you feel good. It’s what all the pharmaceutical companies pump into those wonderful little antidepressants. It’s also a little drug God decided to pump through our brains when we do things he/she/it likes. It’s kinda like a little reward for good behavior, ya know?<br /><br />Here are some of my favorite Big Ideas:<br /><br />1. Serotonin Overdose - Be kind and feel the hit!<br />2. Act “As If” - Your highest says “Hi!” <br />3. Coming to Oneself - The four steps of intention. <br />4. Namaste - I bow to the divine in you. <br />5. Say, “Yes!!” - Say it again! And again! <br /><br />Relax. Embrace the Power of Intention. And have a miraculous day.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />Here's my video review:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YC1zFC3QViw">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YC1zF...</a><br /><br />And click here to find 250+ more of my reviews:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/BrianReviews">http://bit.ly/BrianReviews</a><br /><br />Brian</span>

<div id="review_549481866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/549481866" />
    <a title="Kat McKay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8740144-kat-mckay"><img alt="Kat McKay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343924398p2/8740144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/549481866?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat McKay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat McKay" href="/user/show/8740144-kat-mckay">Kat McKay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781401902179" href="/book/show/1104932.The_Power_of_Intention">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer549481866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7424567797354295092">I love Dr. Dyer! I often find myself going back and listening to his audiobooks a second and 3rd time because they make me feel so much better. His message is inspirational and it's like listening to a loving father when he tells it. There's nothing I hate more than self help gurus that yell at you to get there message across, which to me, is contradictory. Dr. Dyer is NOTHING like that! You feel like you're being guided by a loving and caring friend who truly wants you to be your best self and </span>
  <span id="freeText7424567797354295092" style="display:none">I love Dr. Dyer! I often find myself going back and listening to his audiobooks a second and 3rd time because they make me feel so much better. His message is inspirational and it's like listening to a loving father when he tells it. There's nothing I hate more than self help gurus that yell at you to get there message across, which to me, is contradictory. Dr. Dyer is NOTHING like that! You feel like you're being guided by a loving and caring friend who truly wants you to be your best self and live a life of happiness. I also appreciate that he's not "Christian" centric. Yes, he does quote from Jesus and the Bible, but not in a you-must-conform-to-my-religion way. He also quotes from Buddha and Krishna (but not in this book that I recall, in others he has), famous writers and thinkers, etc. His message is more of universal spirituality. <br /><br />The book itself explains how to set your intentions, keep in tune with them and use them to achieve your goals. Here refers to several different ways of doing this, such as meditation, using positive thoughts and feelings on a daily basis, etc. and backs it up with personal stories as well as those stories of others. <br /><br />I wish I could meet him!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7424567797354295092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32917418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10943703201737218983">I have always enjoyed Wayne Dyer's stuff even if he isn't sure if God is female or not.... Anyway, as he has gotten older his stuff has become more spiritual. He is definitely centered in a higher being and although he seems to be against organized religion I listen to his stuff knowing who my Source is and am grateful for his outspoken belief in God and reminders of the Power we have within and around us. I listened to it as a book on tape and it was definitely worth it.</span>

<div id="review_90103188" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90103188" />
    <a title="PlatKat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/359130-platkat"><img alt="PlatKat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189180079p2/359130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90103188?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PlatKat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PlatKat" href="/user/show/359130-platkat">PlatKat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to PlatKat by: </span>
      Frank
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90103188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9422658100843845383">Frank lent me this book to make use of the first few days of February I spent waiting in his garage for my car to be finished. Somewhat surprisingly, it has opened me up a little despite some of the over-the-top metaphysical discussions. As with all self-help books, you take away the parts you find meaningful to you and let the rest dispose of itself.<br/><br/>Upon finishing this book, I was amazed at the sort of impact it had on my inner-monologue. The main message is that you create your own reality wit</span>
  <span id="freeText9422658100843845383" style="display:none">Frank lent me this book to make use of the first few days of February I spent waiting in his garage for my car to be finished. Somewhat surprisingly, it has opened me up a little despite some of the over-the-top metaphysical discussions. As with all self-help books, you take away the parts you find meaningful to you and let the rest dispose of itself.<br /><br />Upon finishing this book, I was amazed at the sort of impact it had on my inner-monologue. The main message is that you create your own reality with your thoughts and actions. While I already knew this, putting it into practice is a little trickier. Sometimes reading a whole book to confirm what you already know is what it takes to put ideas into action.<br /><br />Like some other books I've read recently, The Power of Intention serves as a reminder to be privy to outside conditions and how they might affect our moods and well being. Eating too much food, overdoing it with caffeine and alcohol, letting loud TVs and music interrupt our peace, and associating with toxic people can have larger effects than we can imagine on how we treat others and view ourselves.<br /><br />We have to train ourselves to be of the mindset the conditions we want are already present. There is an abundance of goodness in this world, and the only thing that keeps us from seeing it are the thoughts we create. I like that he points out in no uncertain terms that stress and anxiety don't "attack" us as we've been conditioned by society to believe, but we create those feelings from our own worries and self-doubt. <br /><br />Sometimes we question ourselves, and that's normal, but overall mental strength is rooted in positivity. He mentions the possibility that sometimes you have to think about your unimportance to realize your value. You don't have to walk around with a stupid smile plastered on your face reciting Stuart Smalley 24/7 to be positive. The effort lies more in balancing the good and bad, then having the confidence to act with kindness and good intentions.<br /><br />Speaking of the word for which the book is titled, the author goes into the meaning of "intention" quite a bit and in a way I didn't expect. He believes we are all connected to the Source, which I interpreted him to mean is sort of an underlying rhythm of the universe that has already decided that good things are in store for us. Contrary to the arguments of many, this goes hand-in-hand with free will.<br /><br />At one point, he goes into the equation of how much energy there is in the world, and how certain people can combat the negative energy of tens, even hundreds, of thousands of people. To me, it just sounded like someone got off on an existential tear one late night, but if that's how some people want to make sense of the world, bully for them.<br /><br />Overall, this book inspired some tremendously insightful and useful feelings in me as I start my business and enter a new phase of my life. Oftentimes, I would put this book down feeling like a million bucks, like I could do anything. Even better, the author actually outlines some good ways to actually do the "anything" that your heart so desires. At some point, I'm going to have to give this book back, but in the meantime, I plan to refer to it when needed, and I would consider buying more books from this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9422658100843845383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

When I first started with it I thought that it was about setting the right intentions in life for one's actions and how "the universe" will give you back accordingly, much like the law of attraction.   <span id="freeText8359807745998630709" style="display:none">I write this review as I reach page 84. This book is blowing me away. When I first started with it I thought that it was about setting the right intentions in life for one's actions and how "the universe" will give you back accordingly, much like the law of attraction. Although this is partly true, the book uses the term "the power of intention" to refer to God. The book is really about the fact that in life you have a willpower to choose to believe in One God or not (the book doesn't explicitly says that, but you'll read it between the lines), and once you made that choice, you should hand all of your life to God and rely on Him to set the course of your life (tawakkol). This is where true happiness is. It also discusses the ego, how to let go of it and how it hinders the connection with God.<br />At the end of each chapter, the book offers practical tips to apply its concepts. <br />This book is a treasure. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618609125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4311231542917362145">This is one of those books you keep near your bedside for late night reading so you can fall asleep after cramming your mind with all these positive thoughts and affirmations, and feel-good thinking. That way, after your unconscious continues to play with the ideas to help you fashion the new you in your dreams, you can awaken the next morning in a very “born again” manner.<br/>	<br/>Perhaps for that reason, it’s also one of those books that might take you six months or more to read, as it’s a form of spi</span>
  <span id="freeText4311231542917362145" style="display:none">This is one of those books you keep near your bedside for late night reading so you can fall asleep after cramming your mind with all these positive thoughts and affirmations, and feel-good thinking. That way, after your unconscious continues to play with the ideas to help you fashion the new you in your dreams, you can awaken the next morning in a very “born again” manner.<br />	<br />Perhaps for that reason, it’s also one of those books that might take you six months or more to read, as it’s a form of spiritual medicine perhaps best appreciated in small doses. Which is not to say you can’t sprint through the book, but it’s been my experience that Dwayne’s books are better for daily tune-ups, served up in small bite size chunks than read end to end in one sitting. But that’s just me. <br />	<br />I prefer to take one of the many brilliant thesis-like ideas in the book, presented in one or two paragraphs and meditate and reflect on that for a few days. But however you get through The Power of Intention, it’s time well spent. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4311231542917362145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9417096219767640408" style="display:none">I have read this book three times! Now I am on the fourth. I love this book; in fact, it changed my life! It is all about working with the Holy Spirit, or the Light of Christ--as the author labels it: the Power of Intention. It's about working on a higher energy level, losing your own ego, and doing what you were intended to do, thereby finding peace and happiness and fulfillment without a huge struggle of massive self-discipline but more of a "let go and let God" effort. It isn't really different from what the scriptures and the prophets teach, but since it's coming from a different direction, it gave me a fresh and enlightened perspective on those things I wasn't really "getting" in my study of the gospel, so now I understand them much better.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9622573713353537156">I have just finished The Power of Intention by Dr Wayne Dyer and I must admit that it has left me more confused than when I started. Firstly let me say that although I have come across quotes from him I have never read any of his book. I thought I would remedy that and this book with it’s brightly coloured pages caught my eye.<br/><br/>So where do I begin? The Power of Intention, also known as ‘the Source’ is an invisible power that we all.connected too. We can call on the power of intention by being posi</span>
  <span id="freeText9622573713353537156" style="display:none">I have just finished The Power of Intention by Dr Wayne Dyer and I must admit that it has left me more confused than when I started. Firstly let me say that although I have come across quotes from him I have never read any of his book. I thought I would remedy that and this book with it’s brightly coloured pages caught my eye.<br /><br />So where do I begin? The Power of Intention, also known as ‘the Source’ is an invisible power that we all.connected too. We can call on the power of intention by being positive and living as if we have already received what the source knows we are already entitled too. However if we are continually negative in our thoughts and action then the source will react to the way we are feeling. Dyer states that we can access the power of intention by using meditation and showing gratitude for what we have, these are two of the ways he mentions there are others in the book.<br /><br />There were parts of this book I felt enraptured by but there were others that were repetitively boring, almost brain-washing it its repetitiveness. Things I agreed with were that when we are not physical we are spiritual, in other words after this life we don’t just disappear we change. That life is eternal. That there is a power greater than us and we can have access to it by the way we live our lives. Also that when those we knew here die and go to the other side they are still cheering us on – so to speak.<br /><br />The biggest negative for me was it’s repetitiveness. As for the rest, maybe it’s just me but I think he would have done better to name The Source, which he doesn't. I do intend to try and get a friend to read and get a second opinion or may you have read it?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9622573713353537156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13965744925580645474">Most of my books reviews will have this disclaimer. Most of the books in my library are audiobooks. I prefer audiobooks especially on long trips. I feel that if the book is that bad at least my time was not a complete waste. With that said I have been following Dr. Dyer on PBS for years. I can always walk away with some good thought or quote. This book was organized but I sometimes loose interest because there is alot to grasp. He is long winded and takes alot of time to make his point. Dr. Dyer</span>
  <span id="freeText13965744925580645474" style="display:none">Most of my books reviews will have this disclaimer. Most of the books in my library are audiobooks. I prefer audiobooks especially on long trips. I feel that if the book is that bad at least my time was not a complete waste. With that said I have been following Dr. Dyer on PBS for years. I can always walk away with some good thought or quote. This book was organized but I sometimes loose interest because there is alot to grasp. He is long winded and takes alot of time to make his point. Dr. Dyer comes across as spiritual but tries to tone it down I guess for his worldly audience. One example of Christian thinking is the prayer of St. Francis and says it is a synonym of God. I also like how Dr. Dyer explains the 7 faces of intention. Creativity, Kindness, Love, Beauty, Expansion, Unlimited Abundance and Receptivity. For example he says "What else can the creator be than Beauty. Beautiful thoughts build a beautiful soul and Beauty is always present even when others see non Beauty." I wouldn't classify Dr. Dyer as New Age because he is close to the mainstream but he does introduce other religions and likes to quote past religious leaders and authors. I would recommend the paper book because I found myself taking lots of notes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13965744925580645474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3362810234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3362810234" />
    <a title="Kushagra Singh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34283553-kushagra-singh"><img alt="Kushagra Singh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588186051p2/34283553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3362810234?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kushagra Singh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kushagra Singh" href="/user/show/34283553-kushagra-singh">Kushagra Singh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19225583-the-power-of-intention">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3362810234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11029106847065000109">I had this book in my wish list since the past couple of years, I think. The title, the author and the cover had attracted me towards it though somehow I didn’t purchase it. <br/><br/>I’m happy that the universe manifested this book for me at what I believe is a perfect time. <br/><br/>Dr Wayne is an inspirational spiritual teacher. He has left his mortal body, but his work continues to inspire many like me to re-connect to the power of the spirit that is the source of all. <br/><br/>Since the beginning of 2020, I have often</span>
  <span id="freeText11029106847065000109" style="display:none">I had this book in my wish list since the past couple of years, I think. The title, the author and the cover had attracted me towards it though somehow I didn’t purchase it. <br /><br />I’m happy that the universe manifested this book for me at what I believe is a perfect time. <br /><br />Dr Wayne is an inspirational spiritual teacher. He has left his mortal body, but his work continues to inspire many like me to re-connect to the power of the spirit that is the source of all. <br /><br />Since the beginning of 2020, I have often had the blessing to hear his talks and conversations with people. Every content of his reflects wisdom, clarity, the profoundness of personal experience and intention of purpose to live a spiritual life. <br /><br />I misjudged this book to be a book on the law of attraction, but, it’s not just about manifesting your desires; the book has profoundly enriching philosophy and profound wisdom to live a good life. <br /><br />I’m so mellowed and positively charged getting the company of Dr Dyer through this book and his words. I did not plan on completing the book within a few days of starting it. However, the book had me hooked onto it, and I completed it a few sittings. <br /><br />The inherent theme of the book is the cultivation of faith and active connection to what we call the source of all- spirit. The book is a motivational document to rekindle the link to that from which we’ve emerged. Once you’re able to do that, manifestation is a piece of cake :) <br /><br />Recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11029106847065000109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2242170547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242170547" />
    <a title="Lynne Fisher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68361343-lynne-fisher"><img alt="Lynne Fisher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590229378p2/68361343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2242170547?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynne Fisher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynne Fisher" href="/user/show/68361343-lynne-fisher">Lynne Fisher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2242170547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1350375052445712117">I haven't read a Wayne Dyer book since the eighties, namely, 'Pulling You Own Strings', which I loved and I have always remembered his advice in this particular book to be creatively alive in any situation, which has served me well. So it was with great hope that I approached the reading of The Power of Intention.<br/><br/>But at the risk of being judged as stubbornly 'resistant' to the philosophies on how to live one's life, I have to say I was disappointed. I understand the principles of what Dyer is ad</span>
  <span id="freeText1350375052445712117" style="display:none">I haven't read a Wayne Dyer book since the eighties, namely, 'Pulling You Own Strings', which I loved and I have always remembered his advice in this particular book to be creatively alive in any situation, which has served me well. So it was with great hope that I approached the reading of The Power of Intention.<br /><br />But at the risk of being judged as stubbornly 'resistant' to the philosophies on how to live one's life, I have to say I was disappointed. I understand the principles of what Dyer is advocating, but I had problems with the word 'Intention', where I began substituting 'universal spirit' instead. I also believe in the power of nature and that of positivity as well as maintaining high energy vibes, but I struggled with the simplistic thinking that if we all tune into the eternal abundance and power of 'Intention' that we will naturally attract good things to come our way, including happiness and worldy success. I've often been called naive in my life, but I can't go as far as to take on Dyer's guarantees (and he does guarantee it) that if we follow his suggestions, all will be well, we will be able to heal ourselves and others and tap into the source of genius while we're at it, and not have to worry about money along the way. What happens to people if they follow all this advice as best they're able and then find it not delivering? Aren't they going to feel like abject failures? Castigate themselves for not connecting properly to the power of intention? But these thoughts all too neatly (for me) feed into the idea of negative resistance, and that feels just a little too convenient.<br /><br />The content was a little too repetitive and confusingly complex at times, and I couldn't wait to get to the end of the book, because I was finding it boggy. And for a book of this genre, you really don't want or need that.<br /><br /> I do give it three stars. Why? Because the advice about what really counts in life, with the pursuit of your bliss, while demonstrating kindness and caring towards others is, I believe, what really counts. But I do the three stars a bit reluctantly and with disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1350375052445712117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tX1RSwmW4/iRlN3lZr/3AkvRoiIDEWqJWrF2Z4GUQ5GT4IvPzKSl82ZchZ6Gc8nFDLVLQKfTQRKiSibA/KNk2w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12823937353191825494">Wayne Walter Dyer was a popular American self-help advocate, author and lecturer. His 1976 book Your Erroneous Zones has sold over 30 million copies and is one of the best-selling books of all time. It is said to have "[brought] humanistic ideas to the masses".<br/><br/>He received his D.Ed. degree in counseling from Wayne State University. He was a guidance counselor in Detroit at the high school level and</span>
  <span id="freeText12823937353191825494" style="display:none">Wayne Walter Dyer was a popular American self-help advocate, author and lecturer. His 1976 book Your Erroneous Zones has sold over 30 million copies and is one of the best-selling books of all time. It is said to have "[brought] humanistic ideas to the masses".<br /><br />He received his D.Ed. degree in counseling from Wayne State University. He was a guidance counselor in Detroit at the high school level and a professor of counselor education at St. John's University in New York.<br />He first pursued an academic career, publishing in journals and running a successful private therapy practice, but his lectures at St. John's, which focused on positive thinking and motivational speaking techniques, attracted students beyond those enrolled. A literary agent persuaded Dyer to package his ideas in book form, resulting in Your Erroneous Zones; although initial sales were thin, Dyer quit his teaching job and began a publicity tour of the United States, doggedly pursuing bookstore appearances and media interviews ("out of the back of his station wagon", according to Michael Korda, making the best-seller lists "before book publishers even noticed what was happening"</span>
